(A, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَثْوِيبٌ</foreign> meaning The <hi rend="ital">calling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">summoning,</hi> (M, Mgh, K,) <hi rend="ital">to prayer,</hi> (M, K,) and <hi rend="ital">to other things,</hi> (M,) is said to be from <foreign lang="ar">ثَوْبٌ</foreign> “ a garment, ” (Mgh,) because a man, when he comes crying out for aid, makes a sign with his garment, (M, Mgh,) moving it about, raising his hand with it, in order that he to whom he calls may see it, (Mgh,) and this action is like a calling, or summoning, (M, Mgh,) and an announcing, to him; so the calling, or summoning, by reason to frequent usage of this word [as meaning the <hi rend="ital">making a sign with a garment</hi>], came to be thus called; and one said of the caller, or summoner, <foreign lang="ar">ثوَب</foreign>: (Mgh:) or it means the <hi rend="ital">calling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">summoning, twice;</hi> (M, K;) or the <hi rend="ital">repeating a call</hi> or <hi rend="ital">summons;</hi> from <foreign lang="ar">ثاب</foreign> “ he returned: ” (Mgh:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">ثوّب</foreign>, inf. n. as above, (T, Msb,) meaning <hi rend="ital">he called,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">summoned, one time after another;</hi> (T;) <hi rend="ital">he repeated his call,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cry:</hi> (Msb:) and hence <foreign lang="ar">تثويب</foreign> in the <foreign lang="ar">أَذَان</foreign>; (T, Msb;) i. e., the <hi rend="ital">saying</hi> of the <foreign lang="ar">مُؤَذِّن</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">after having, by the</hi>

                  <hi rend="ital">A garment,</hi> (M, Mgh, Msb, K,) [or <hi rend="ital">piece of cloth</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stuff,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that is worn by men, composed of linen, cotton, wool, fur,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَزّ</foreign> [q. v.], (Mgh, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">silk,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like;</hi> (Msb;) but [properly] <hi rend="ital">not what is cut out of several pieces, such as the shirt, and trousers, or drawers, &amp;c.;</hi> (Mgh;) [though often applied to a shirt or shift (<foreign lang="ar">قَمِيص</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">دِرْع</foreign>) and to a <foreign lang="ar">جُبَّة</foreign> &amp;c.:] it seems to be so called because the wearer returns to it, or it to the wearer, time after time: (Mgh:) [also <hi rend="ital">a garment worn by women and girls over the shift;</hi> (see <foreign lang="ar">أُصْدَةٌ</foreign>;) app., as in the present day, <hi rend="ital">a long gown, reaching to the feet, with very wide sleeves:</hi>] pl. <foreign lang="ar">ثِيَابٌ</foreign> [the pl. of mult.] (T, S, M, A, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَثْوَابٌ</foreign> [a pl. of pauc.] (S, M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَثْوُبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَثْؤُبٌ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) the last two being pls. of pauc., and the latter of them being thus pronounced with <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> by some of the Arabs because the dammeh immediately after <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> is deemed difficult of utterance; for which reason they substitute <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> in all instances like this.                   </form> The <hi rend="ital">place where the water collects in a valley or low ground;</hi> so called because the water returns to it: (Aboo-Kheyreh, T:) and the <hi rend="ital">middle</hi> of a watering-trough or tank, (T, S, M,) <hi rend="ital">to which the water returns when it has been emptied,</hi> (S,) or <hi rend="ital">to which what remains of the water returns;</hi> (T;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n4804-1" target="مَثَابٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n4813"/></foreign>: (S:) the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> is a substitute for the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>, the medial radical, which is suppressed; (S, L;) the word being from <foreign lang="ar">ثَابَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَثُوبُ</foreign>: (L:) Aboo-Is-hák infers that this is the case from its having for its dim.
